<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b2856c30-4f41-41f9-a70a-fe056e30f3e0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText12382098082090646094" style="display:none">In this third book in the Lunar Chronicles, Cinder and Captain Thorne are fugitives on the run, now with Scarlet and Wolf in tow. Together, they're plotting to overthrow Queen Levana and her army.<br /><br />Their best hope lies with Cress, a girl imprisoned on a satellite since childhood who's only ever had her netscreens as company. All that screen time has made Cress an excellent hacker. Unfortunately, she's just received orders from Levana to track down Cinder and her handsome accomplice.<br /><br />When a daring rescue of Cress goes awry, the group is separated. Cress finally has her freedom, but it comes at a higher price. Meanwhile, Queen Levana will let nothing prevent her marriage to Emperor Kai. Cress, Scarlet, and Cinder may not have signed up to save the world, but they may be the only hope the world has.</span>

<div id="review_493120234" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/493120234" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4152659-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346808389p2/4152659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/493120234?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/4152659-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4152659-anne?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer493120234&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer493120234" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10452596743621893956"><b>***BEFORE READING</b><br/><br/>OH. MY. GOD I THINK I HAVE MADE A MIRACULOUS DISCOVERY!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403191ra/784325.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>So, I was re-reading Cinder when I came upon the part where Dr. Erland is explaining why he hates the Queen so much and it's because his daughter-who is a shell- was supposedly murdered by the Queen. His daughters name is Crescent Moon. <b>CRESCENT MOON. CRESCENT SHORT FOR CRESS BY ANY CHANCE</b> !<br/><br/>That was not my only discovery but, we all know that the 4th book called Winter will be about Snow White. Does anyone else remember in </span>
  <span id="freeText10452596743621893956" style="display:none"><b>***BEFORE READING</b><br><br>OH. MY. GOD I THINK I HAVE MADE A MIRACULOUS DISCOVERY!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403191ra/784325.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So, I was re-reading Cinder when I came upon the part where Dr. Erland is explaining why he hates the Queen so much and it's because his daughter-who is a shell- was supposedly murdered by the Queen. His daughters name is Crescent Moon. <b>CRESCENT MOON. CRESCENT SHORT FOR CRESS BY ANY CHANCE</b> !<br><br>That was not my only discovery but, we all know that the 4th book called Winter will be about Snow White. Does anyone else remember in the beginning where Cinder was talking about all the rumors about the Queen and said<b> "They said she forced her stepdaughter to mutilate her own face because, at the sweet age of thirteen, she had become more beautiful than the jealous queen could stand" MIRROR MIRROR ON THE WALL WHOSE THE FAIREST OF THEM ALL? .</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403191ra/784326.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><s>I may be wrong this is just a guess</s><br><br><b>***AFTER READING</b><br><br>Oh my ... This book was just am-.... Characters were absolutely incre- .... Plot was spot o-....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391649409ra/8425582.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Seriously I don't even know where to begin this review for this undeniable master piece of a novel. For one, it totally lived up to every single one of my expectations which was pretty surprising since I had such high expectations; there's nothing worse then hyping up a novel/movie/event so much that when you do read/watch/go to it , it's all a bit anti climatic because of all these impractical hopes you had. So when I did read Cress I was in absolute awe on how much I loved it. <br><br>The characters were all so dearly loveable and each one of them had a clear distinct personality. Thus when reading all the different point of views you could clearly distinguish a unique voice making each chapter a refreshing breath of new air. As for the new characters Cress was a brilliant actress in the making and captured the dreamer inside of us all perfectly. I particularly adored how Meyer made <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Cress totally idealize Thorne. Took away the fabricated fascination. Yet, she still had the ability to make Thorne perfectly imperfect.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I even loved to hate Levanna and I just cant wait for the next installment where we get to learn more of her back story. That being said can we all talk about that little sneak peek we got on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Winters character. I totally can't wait to read more about her with her <s>captivating</s>"crazy" talk of walls bleeding and describing smiles as sunrises. Can it just be 2015 already?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I could literally write an essay on every single character on why their magnificent and why I love them but... that would make this review a bit dull and mundane so I'll leave the essay writing for English. <br><br>The plot was fast paced with not a dull moment to be seen. It was filled with adventure: treks through the dessert, hopeless situations,(not so) damsels in distress, battles and small dashes of romance that spontaneously made me have a stupid, goofy grin.<br><br>All in all Cress was a steller novel filled with twists and turns and the power to enchant readers reminding them of the oh so familiar fairytale: Rapunzel. <br><br>Me reading all the swoon worthy romance bits <b> *cough cough Cinder and Kai cough cough*<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391652738ra/8426111.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Me reading everything else <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380431191ra/865112.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>(Also addressing my prediction <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ YES! YES! YES! YES! I TOTALLY KNEW IT! *breaks out into a little happy dance* Also another cool bit of trivia I saw off tumblr is that you can even see the little Cresent in the 'C' of Cress. There's so much foreshadowing in this series. Ugh. I love it. I seriously love the Lunar Chronicles so much! And thanks again to everyone with their comments regarding the prediction and especially a shout out to the ones who called me a 'genius'. The real 'genius' is obviously Marissa Meyer herself and calling me one is far off from the truth however, it is one hell of an ego boost ;) So thanks again!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></b><br><br>Side note: I've received a few messages concerning the prediction part of my review - due to it actually becoming true I should mark it as a spoiler. Many apologies in advance for unintentionally spoiling Cress. I seriously made that prediction a long, long, LONG time ago ... like before Scarlet even came out and never thought about it from the perspective of fresh eyes. So once again, sorry. <br><br><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_793673146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793673146" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793673146?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793673146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4373164566038805138"><blockquote>
  <i>“Have you given any thought to your wedding vows?” Kai snorted. <br/>“Delete anything that has to do with love, respect, or joy, and I’ll sign on the dotted line.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>3 1/2 stars. After I finally gave in and read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206760.Scarlet__The_Lunar_Chronicles___2_' title='Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scarlet</a> recently, people have been urging me to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206828.Cress__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_' title='Cress (The Lunar Chronicles, #3) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cress</a>. I can see why - this book is so so much fun.<br/><br/>Firstly, I have to say that Meyer has really worked on her pacing since the days of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_' title='Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinder</a> (which I personally found really boring). This book zips along from action scene, to discovery, t</span>
  <span id="freeText4373164566038805138" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Have you given any thought to your wedding vows?” Kai snorted. <br />“Delete anything that has to do with love, respect, or joy, and I’ll sign on the dotted line.”</i>
</blockquote><br />3 1/2 stars. After I finally gave in and read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206760.Scarlet__The_Lunar_Chronicles___2_" title="Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a> recently, people have been urging me to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206828.Cress__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_" title="Cress (The Lunar Chronicles, #3) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cress</a>. I can see why - this book is so so much fun.<br /><br />Firstly, I have to say that Meyer has really worked on her pacing since the days of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a> (which I personally found really boring). This book zips along from action scene, to discovery, to maybe romance and all of it is pretty well-balanced. <b>It's not high literature, but it <i>is</i> pure enjoyment.</b><br /><br />In this book, we get to know Cress - a girl locked away by herself in a spaceship and based on the fairy tale character Rapunzel. While completely different from the level-headed Cinder or the fiery Scarlet, Cress is <b>absolutely lovable</b>. I usually tend to find myself liking stronger, more cynical characters, but Cress' naivete is both realistic and completely charming.<br /><br />In fact, this is the funniest book yet, with lots of humourous banter to balance out the plagues, near death experiences, and evil bitch queens. <br /><br />The author pokes fun at instalove and silly, romantic obsession, portraying Cress as a sheltered girl with unrealistic romantic expectations suddenly receiving a cold hard shock as she enters the real world and finds that eyes do not simply meet across crowded rooms.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You want to know another secret? The biggest secret? I’m scared, Kai. I’m so scared.”</i>
</blockquote><br />As well as the light entertainment, things are also getting serious. My sympathy for Kai and his unfortunate situation increases with every book, and I like Cinder more when she is not the sole focus of the story. And I'd just like to say that there is something really exciting about the psychotic villains of this series (hence why I had to pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22489107.Fairest__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_5_" title="Fairest (The Lunar Chronicles, #3.5) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a> right away).<br /><br />But mostly, <b>I think I am just in love with Captain Thorne</b>. He's such an hilarious, unconventional love interest and I welcome every scene he is in. He kind of gives off a Gilderoy Lockhart vibe - good-looking, self-obsessed, lovable and so full of it. His comments in dire situations had me laughing out loud.<br /><br />That's all for now. I need to go read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22489107.Fairest__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_5_" title="Fairest (The Lunar Chronicles, #3.5) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairest</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a>. It looks like all kinds of crazy has been set up for the next book.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4373164566038805138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1183237156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183237156" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1183237156?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1183237156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6500786393766264241"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Even in the Future the Story Begins with Once Upon a Time.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Once Upon a Time</b>, there was an avid reader (let's call her Teri) who lived and breathed words. When she was sad, she bought a book to cheer her up. When she was happy or successful, she bought a book to celebrate. When she was worried, she bought a book to forget her problems. One cold winter's night, she found herself in a magical place known as the Bookstore. A place full of wonders and fairydust, a safe haven from a world</span>
  <span id="freeText6500786393766264241" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Even in the Future the Story Begins with Once Upon a Time.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Once Upon a Time</b>, there was an avid reader (let's call her Teri) who lived and breathed words. When she was sad, she bought a book to cheer her up. When she was happy or successful, she bought a book to celebrate. When she was worried, she bought a book to forget her problems. One cold winter's night, she found herself in a magical place known as the Bookstore. A place full of wonders and fairydust, a safe haven from a world so mundane and self-destructive. A place to be herself. She spent hours strolling in the corridors illuminated by the brilliance of Luna, and when she left she took a piece of Luna with her. She took <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206828.Cress__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_" title="Cress (The Lunar Chronicles, #3) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cress</a>.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I promise, I will not let you die without being kissed.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395112622ra/8948142.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>After Cinderella and Red Riding Hood, it was <b>Rapunzel</b>'s time to contribute to the interplanetary efforts to ger rid of Evil Queen Levana and her bloodthirsty minions whose only life purpose was world domination and extermination of mankind. And Cress' story reminded Teri so much of Disney's <b>Tangled</b> that she kept trying-and failed-to supress the urge to squeal (she will get angry if she finds out I told you this but she's watched Tangled more than <s>five</s> ten times). When Cress crossed paths with the crew of Rampion and everything went to Hell, Teri wasn't sure whose story she wanted to follow the most: Kai's decent attempts to make peace with his painful but noble decision, Cress and Thorne's adventures in the desert, Scarlet's struggles to survive, or Cinder and Wolf's journey and their unlikely alliance with Jacin? Each chapter had <b>magnetic powers with a hint of compulsion</b>, and Teri's heart was ready to <b>explode</b> from the emotions that kept piling up. Every feeling was a star and together they shaped a constellation so bright that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4684322.Marissa_Meyer" title="Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Marissa Meyer</a> could see it from her house and admire the effect of her work. If she also rubbed her hands in a villain fashion, that I cannot tell.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Maybe there isn’t such a thing as fate. Maybe it’s just the opportunities we’re given, and what we do with them. I’m beginning to think that maybe great, epic romances don’t just happen. We have to make them ourselves.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Teri wasn't sure if she liked Cress. She was really naive, really childish and her fantasies were wilder than her hair. But Teri couldn't help but admit that <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4684322.Marissa_Meyer" title="Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Marissa Meyer</a>'s ability to paint so many different yet interesting characters</b> was admirable. There were no similarities between Cinder, Scarlet and Cress besides the fact that their destinies were interwined, that the fate of Earth and Luna would be determined by their joint efforts and sacrifices. The <b>diversity and complexity of the female characters</b>, the <b>smart humour</b>, the <b>sassiness</b>, the <b>suspense</b>, the <b>action</b> and the <b>unpredictable turns</b> of the events made <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206828.Cress__The_Lunar_Chronicles___3_" title="Cress (The Lunar Chronicles, #3) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cress</a> such an addictive book. And the <b>swoonworthy male leads</b>. And the <b>sweet, innocent and pure romance</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383605016ra/6608808.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Teri was <b>in love with Thorne</b>. His attempts to convince Cress that he was no hero or a good man but instead an opportunist thief that treated everything as a big joke failed when he showed compassion and kindness. He was lost, but he had a hero quality that no one can question. There was also Wolf. Shy and awkward and scary and savage Wolf that loved Scarlet so much that made Teri weak in the knees.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451787651ra/17604913.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Kai who was torn between his hope that Cinder actually cared for him and his anger for everything that happened is one of the characters that hold your heart and you don't even realize it. And finally Jacin, who is cryptic and kind of an asshole but Teri is positive she'll fall for him in the next book. But even though Thorne is Teri's favorite male character, Scarlet her favorite female character, Scarlet/Wolf her favorite ship, <b>the entire gang, their banters and their loyalty and friendship is after all the main reason the Lunar Chronicles is a series so special</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449535646ra/17298783.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>P.S. Wanna bet who is Teri?<br><br>✨ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183237483?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder review</a><br>✨ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183237129?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet review</a><br>✨ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1153134052?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter review</a><br>✨ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1741314666?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Stars Above review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6500786393766264241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2197881027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2197881027" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2197881027?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2197881027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6504816000198191905"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536067108i/26251235._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>Maybe great, epic romances don't just happen. We have to make them ourselves.</i>
</blockquote><b>Fun, lighthearted and delightful. </b> I absolutely love how each book in this series is better than the last! <br/><br/>As with the previous two, we have a <b> fairytale themed futuristic dystopian adventure.</b> While each book follows a different couple, we get to catch up on the previous ones and get hints at the new. <br/><br/>This one focuses on Cress (Rapunzel). She's a "Shell" (a Lunar who is immune to Lunar glamours). <br/><br/>She's spen</span>
  <span id="freeText6504816000198191905" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536067108i/26251235._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>Maybe great, epic romances don't just happen. We have to make them ourselves.</i>
</blockquote><b>Fun, lighthearted and delightful. </b> I absolutely love how each book in this series is better than the last! <br><br>As with the previous two, we have a <b> fairytale themed futuristic dystopian adventure.</b> While each book follows a different couple, we get to catch up on the previous ones and get hints at the new. <br><br>This one focuses on Cress (Rapunzel). She's a "Shell" (a Lunar who is immune to Lunar glamours). <br><br>She's spent her entire life in a satellite in orbit and while her<b> isolation drives her a bit mad, </b> but hey, at least she has the internet.<br><br>And on that internet, she discovers Thorne - excuse me -<b><i> Captain</i> Thorne. </b>He's the daring and dashing hero - the defender of innocents, the savior of all things good and Cress is completely, and irrevocably enthralled.<blockquote>
  <i>“Captain,” she murmured. “I think I’m in love with you." </i>
</blockquote> Finally, Cress makes a harrowing break for freedom and much to her delight, she is accompanied by <i>Captain</i> Thorne. <br><br>Only, she soon discovers that the man she's dreamed of for the last few years is nothing like the man before her.<blockquote>
  <i>A hand landed on Cress’s head. She gasped and recoiled, but Thorne was already wrapping his arm around her shoulders and squeezing her against him. <br>“Just checking it was you,” he whispered. </i>
</blockquote> With the revolution starting and the plague spreading, does Cress even have the time to get to know the real Thorne?<br><br><b>Overall - <u>LOVED it!</u></b><br><br>Cress and Thorne have got to be <b>my favorite couple </b> - I loved her <b>joyful innocence</b> and his <b>blustery confidence</b> cinched them as a couple in my mind. <blockquote>
  <i> “How are your eyes?" she asked.<br>"Well, I've been told they're dreamy, but I'll let you decide for yourself.” </i>
</blockquote>Cress and Thorne have such a <b>natural chemistry.</b> Every time they were "on screen" I was ecstatic! <blockquote>
  <i>“Yeah, I guess you're right," he said, squeezing. "Maybe there's a little bit of a hero in me after all. But... really, Cress. Only a little.” </i>
</blockquote> In addition, I feel like the other couples have gotten stronger - in particular Scarlet and Wolf are really hitting it off. <br><br>However, <b>Cinder &amp; Kai just don't click</b> for me. <br><br>To be fair, they haven't been in the same room for a couple books (I still maintain that Cinder EASILY could've sent him an email and thus completely resolving the issues of book 2 and 3). Hopefully they will be together a bit more later on...?<br><br>Anyway, I really feel like Marissa Meyer has hit her stride in this series - the characters are fabulous, the banter is witty and the plot is just swimming along. I could not be more excited to see how this series turns out! <br><br>P.S. Is it just me or does Iko really need to fall in love!? Give the poor girl a robot boyfriend!<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Read by Rebecca Soler and she was a fabulous reader. Cress sounded so freaking adorable throughout!<br><br>If you are curious about Rebecca Soler, check Tucker the Reader's <a href="https://tuckerthereader.wordpress.com/2019/04/30/interview-with-rebecca-soler/" rel="nofollow noopener"> interview</a>!<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6504816000198191905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_311710212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311710212" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311710212?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone, damn it!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      Myself. Sometimes I get it right.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=addictive-read">addictive-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=smart-heroine">smart-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=print-arc">print-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=macmillan">macmillan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311710212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3859843649100684561">This is my 100th book of 2013 and it was magnificent. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392041720ra/8491305.gif' alt=' photo fireworks_zps17303d64.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>NEED. WINTER. NOW. <br/><br/>When I first jumped on the Lunar Chronicles bandwagon, I was late to the party. I tend to avoid any novel in the blogosphere that is garnering a ton of hype, due to past experiences where the hype completely killed my enjoyment. However, I dove into <i>Cinder</i> trepidatiously and came out completely in love, mostly thanks to the sweet nostalgia feelings from the cleverly added Sailor Moon references. And if that wasn’t clear bef</span>
  <span id="freeText3859843649100684561" style="display:none">This is my 100th book of 2013 and it was magnificent. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392041720ra/8491305.gif" alt=" photo fireworks_zps17303d64.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>NEED. WINTER. NOW. <br><br>When I first jumped on the Lunar Chronicles bandwagon, I was late to the party. I tend to avoid any novel in the blogosphere that is garnering a ton of hype, due to past experiences where the hype completely killed my enjoyment. However, I dove into <i>Cinder</i> trepidatiously and came out completely in love, mostly thanks to the sweet nostalgia feelings from the cleverly added Sailor Moon references. And if that wasn’t clear before, I’m somewhat of a huge Sailor Moon fangirl. Like, it's a little scary. Perhaps you should run?<br><br>Unfortunately, with <i>Scarlet</i>, I didn’t get the same warm fuzzies and I began to worry that this story was simply too big for Meyer to conquer. Don’t get me wrong, I did enjoy Scarlet, but the pacing and connection to the characters didn’t happen for me. It wouldn’t be the first time I read a series where the best book was the first book. So, again, I found myself wary for <i>Cress</i>, but those worries proved to be unnecessary. Ahem, allow me to eat my words.<br><br><i>Cress</i> is a complete improvement over <i>Cinder</i> and <i>Scarlet</i>. Where <i>Cinder</i> had its issues with predictability, <i>Cress</i>’s plot was noticeably tighter. While <i>Scarlet</i> had parts where the pacing felt off due to the dual point of views, <i>Cress</i> kicked it up a few notches with perfectly timed highs and lows. At no point did I find myself bored to tears, banging my head against the wall from frustration, throwing the book across the room, or simply suffering from major disappointment. It’s action-packed, well plotted, and exciting!<br><br>I should probably take this time to mention that if you haven’t read Cinder and Scarlet, 1) it’s time to re-examine your life choices 2) the rest of the review may contain slight spoilers for the first two books. But you should know by now, that's just how I roll.<br><br>The novel begins with the gang (Cinder, Thorne, Scarlet, Wolf, and Iko) on a mission to rescue Cress from her satellite. STUFF happens and things go horribly wrong, causing them to separate. What I loved about this was it gave the reader the perfect opportunity to get to know each individual character in a more intimate manner. Thorne and Cress end up stranded in the Sahara Desert, which is interesting because Cress has never stepped foot on Earth and being isolated for years didn’t exactly grant her the best social skills, and due to certain circumstances on the satellite, Throne is left blind. I didn't like this one bit. How could Meyer do this to my precious Throne?! MY PRECIOUSSS. MY PRECIOUSSS. He is sacred and must not be touched!! Still, it makes for an unlikely team and optimal time for character development and revelations. The only thing that I’m not too sure of is the romance brewing. Why does everyone in this series have to be paired up with someone? There is absolutely nothing wrong with self love. Even Oprah knows this.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392041240ra/8491251.gif" alt=" photo Oprah-Bath-Gif_zps52ec5b11.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>That's probably something you never wanted to see. Welcome to a Steph Sinclair review.</i><br><br>Cinder on the other hand, struggles with decisions that she made on the satellite, ultimately leading to unfortunate outcomes for both Scarlet and Wolf. Can she really do this, lead people and start a rebellion? Should she simply give up and continue hiding from Levana? Is she slowly becoming the very woman whom she fears? She’s conflicted for most of the novel and tends to second guess herself a lot more once she realizes how severe the consequences of her actions can be. Basically, Cinder is no Mary Sue and carries mistakes and flaws just like any other character in this series.<br><br>Scarlet is not as present in Cress, but her role looks like it’ll be more important in the final installment, <i>Winter</i>. I can’t really talk about what Scarlet endures in this novel because I’m tip toeing around a minefield of spoilers here, but I was very surprised to see how far Meyer was willing push her character’s limits. And if you’ve already read <i>Cress</i>, I think you know exactly what scene I’m referring to. Can we say, “SHIT JUST GOT REAL?” I’m resisting the urge to throw in a “Brace Yourself” meme.<br><br>Oh, what the hell!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392040604i/8491156._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo BraceYourself_zpsabbae5b7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I’m left both amazed and impressed with <i>Cress</i>. I can confidently say that this series just gets better and better and I’d consider this my favorite so far. With the sneak peek of the newest character, Winter (she's adorably certifiable), at the end, I’m eagerly waiting for the final book. Gimme, Gimme, Gimme.<br><br><i>An ARC was received from the publisher for an honest review.</i><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddelbuggery</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3859843649100684561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1714742164?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=dystopian-scifi">dystopian-scifi</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1714742164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10128272720015891005">Well THAT was fun. Why. Why did I wait so long to read this series??!<br/><br/><b>Cress. Thorne. Freaking cuteness overload.</b> Yep, I'm going to talk about it because I may or may not have squealed aloud several times while reading this book. They are easily one of my all time favorite ships.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395112622ra/8948142.gif' width='380px' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Cress herself is just so stinking cute. She's so not like a typical heroine. She's extremely intelligent but is primarily a daydreamer and tends to be swept up in her imagination. Ahem... that sounds familiar. Anywayyyy I </span>
  <span id="freeText10128272720015891005" style="display:none">Well THAT was fun. Why. Why did I wait so long to read this series??!<br><br><b>Cress. Thorne. Freaking cuteness overload.</b> Yep, I'm going to talk about it because I may or may not have squealed aloud several times while reading this book. They are easily one of my all time favorite ships.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395112622ra/8948142.gif" width="380px" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cress herself is just so stinking cute. She's so not like a typical heroine. She's extremely intelligent but is primarily a daydreamer and tends to be swept up in her imagination. Ahem... that sounds familiar. Anywayyyy I love how socially awkward and naive she is to the outside world. And Thorne, who is obviously brother from another mother to Nikolai Lansov (Grisha Trilogy) because they are both so completely snarky, cocky, down right hysterical divas.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470178514ra/19898294.gif" width="380px" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So if it isn't already completely obvious- I had some major Cress / Thorne feels and their slow burn actually drove me a little nuts with my impatience. I still need so much more... I enjoyed them SO much. They are so similar the characters in Tangled (but different too!) <br><br>Of course, they tended to take the front seat in this novel but the rest of the characters/storylines were not far behind. This book was definitely action packed and full of fun surprises. Not to mention- the hole left in my heart for Cinder/Kia from book one definitely tugged at me again in this book. Was it resolved? I guess you'll have to see! <br><br>And Iko! I did not expect her to take on a bigger role in this book - but she easily became one of my favorite characters! Such a pleasant surprise.<br><br>The world building is still fairly mediocre to me (nothing super unique) but it was more fun just based on the fact that all the fairytales we grew up with are intertwined. I still fail to see how Levana is anything beyond a typical 'evil' villain. I don't feel strongly about her- I'm hoping she gets more complex. Additionally, while some of the other characters aren't as strong as others, their vastly different personalities kept me intrigued. Plus, the plot was just down right fun. The pacing was perfect in this one.<br><br><b>Do I recommend this series?</b> Heck yeah I do. So far all three books have been light and fun while still managing to get some pretty strong emotions out of me. It's been a nice change of pace for me - a refreshing break from my average fantasy reads. <br><br>SOOO here I go to book four- I'm hoping it doesn't disappoint because <b>I STILL need so much resolution for my ships!!</b><br><br><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1348947342?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1348947342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15303883053680710345">MY LONGEST YEAH BOI EVER.<br/><br/>This review only really needs to be two sentences long. Here are those sentences:<br/>1) This book has Cress.<br/>2) This book has Thorne.<br/><br/>End review.<br/><br/>As everyone knows because I never shut up about it for even one second, I don’t love characters very often. It just takes a lot for me to be Interested. But these two...these two.<br/><br/>I am a currently living human being (hard as that may be to believe), and that means I love heists. If there is a better trope than the heist plotline, I kno</span>
  <span id="freeText15303883053680710345" style="display:none">MY LONGEST YEAH BOI EVER.<br /><br />This review only really needs to be two sentences long. Here are those sentences:<br />1) This book has Cress.<br />2) This book has Thorne.<br /><br />End review.<br /><br />As everyone knows because I never shut up about it for even one second, I don’t love characters very often. It just takes a lot for me to be Interested. But these two...these two.<br /><br />I am a currently living human being (hard as that may be to believe), and that means I love heists. If there is a better trope than the heist plotline, I know not of it, and honestly I don’t care to know it because I may be overwhelmed by Goodness. Heists are the most fun, and roughly 45 to 67 percent of that high level of fun-ness is due to the dope character archetypes. RAGTAG GROUPS OF FUN-LOVING, THIEVING RUFFIANS. <br /><br />This seemingly unrelated paragraph has a point, and the point is this: Both Cress and Thorne are archetypes straight out of a heist.<br /><br />Cress is The Hacker. Hackers are so fun and ridiculous that I firmly believe they should exist in every story ever. This includes historical fiction, because what could be more fun and ridiculous than that? Picture your favorite pioneer-West story or medieval royalty romance, except with a hacker. Try to tell me that isn’t both ridiculous and fun.<br /><br />You can’t.<br /><br />Thorne is The Charming Rogue. This is a trope that doesn’t always work for me, because even though it is a classic heist archetype, it is also a classic Cringey YA archetype. And since I’m usually reading cringey YA, that’s the feeling that comes through. <br /><br />BUT NOT THIS TIME. Because this time, we have a hacker.<br /><br />I myself can’t picture anything much more fun than well-executed iterations of The Hacker and The Rogue falling in love. Except if there was a heist involved.<br /><br />But that’d just be greedy.<br /><br />Bottom line: I simply don’t care about anything about this book besides Cress And Thorne. Luckily those two are enough in and of themselves.<br /><br />RIDICULOUS AND FUN.<br /><br />---------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />honestly not sure whether I'd rather marry Cress or Thorne. so I'll settle for them marrying each other<br /><br />review to come / 4.5 stars<br /><br />---------<br /><br />I AM READY FOR JOY AND HIJINKS.<br /><br />and this was my favorite book in the series when I first read them, so if I do not get joy and hijinks I will be forced to burn everything to the ground.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15303883053680710345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9794706605557099287"><i>“Her satellite made one full orbit around Planet Earth every sixteen hours. It was a prison that came with an endlessly breathtaking view— vast blue oceans and swirling clouds and sunrises that set half the world on fire.” </i><br/><br/>What more can I possibly say about this series that I haven’t already mentioned in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206760.Scarlet__The_Lunar_Chronicles___2_' title='Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scarlet</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_' title='Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinder</a>?! <br/><br/>- That Marissa Meyer is an auto-buy author?? <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>.<br/>- That her writing makes me <i>feel</i> everything?? <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>.<br/>- That this world made me somehow enjoy its dystopian nature??</span>
  <span id="freeText9794706605557099287" style="display:none"><i>“Her satellite made one full orbit around Planet Earth every sixteen hours. It was a prison that came with an endlessly breathtaking view— vast blue oceans and swirling clouds and sunrises that set half the world on fire.” </i><br><br>What more can I possibly say about this series that I haven’t already mentioned in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206760.Scarlet__The_Lunar_Chronicles___2_" title="Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a>?! <br><br>- That Marissa Meyer is an auto-buy author?? <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>.<br>- That her writing makes me <i>feel</i> everything?? <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>.<br>- That this world made me somehow enjoy its dystopian nature?? <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>.<br>- That I’M ATTACHED TO A CAST OF CHARACTERS LIKE THORNE AND CINDER AND CRESS AND IKO AND WOLF AND SCARLET AND KAI AND AND I NEED TO CALM DOWN?? <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>. <s>sort off</s> <br>- That there are unexpected plot twists and turns?? <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>.<br>- That there are lots of intense, gripping moments?? <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>.<br>- That there are lots of <b>brutal</b> action?? (well to be fair, it only got brutal in the middle? of <i>Scarlet</i>, all the way through to <i>Cress</i>) <i>
  <b>Check</b>
</i>.<br>- (I’m also crying for Wolf because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he called Scarlet his <i>“brightest star”</i>, now that’s so much better than “alpha”. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>)<br><br><b>Will there be a pros and cons list like in the last two reviews?</b> N O. I can’t fault this book for it being everything I wanted, if not more! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496324652ra/22901260.gif" width="500" height="234" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Earth is now in the midst of a war thanks to a whiny child *cough, Levana*. She won’t put an end to it “until” she marries Kai and becomes the empress of New Beijing. Kai has agreed to do so, in exchange for Levana’s cure for Letumosis. Meanwhile, he hasn’t given up on trying to find Princess Selene as she could be the one to finally end Queen Levana’s tyranny.<br><br>On the other hand, we have the <b>squad</b> (Thorne, Cinder, Iko, Scarlet and Wolf), who managed to escape Africa and fly to space using Thorne’s ship (the Rampion). This is where Cress comes to play when the Rampion receives an important message from her. I remember Cress as the “satellite girl” from <i>Cinder</i>, as she was the one that warned Nainsi (Kai’s android) of Levana’s plan to rule Earth. With that said, we uncover that Cress has been stuck in the satellite (in Luna) for <b>7 years</b>, used by Mistress Sybil (Levana’s thaumaturge) for her talent in hacking any system. <br><br>So, this book follows the squad trying to rescue Cress and together, plans to delay Kai’s alliance to Queen Levana. Of course, that’s if they manage to cross many, <s>unfortunate</s> barriers along the way ;) <br><br>I also want to note that we get a little glimpse of <u>Winter</u> towards the end of the book (in preparation for book 4) and she seems really <i>interesting</i>. I’m very excited for it and hope that I won’t be <i>too</i> crushed by the conclusion of this series.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496324652ra/22901259.gif" width="357" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“The other girl, Iko, cupped her chin with both hands. "This is so much better than a net drama.” </i><br><br>---<br><br><b>MORE THORNE??<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495546575ra/22828956.gif" width="500" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'M SO EXCITED FOR THIS, YOU DON'T UNDERSTAND.</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

</p><br/><br/><b> BEFORE READING:</b><br/>Cinder?...and Rapunzel?...in a desert?...in 2014? <br/>Can life get any more depressing?!?!?! It sounds so interesting but also sooooo far away! I just read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17193739.Scarlet__Lunar_Chronicles___2_' title='Scarlet (Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scarlet</a> and now I have to wait a whole year!!!!<br/>It's like....<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399031ra/771725.gif' width='' height='' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>(was that the perfect gif or what?)<br/><br/>Oh and Scarlet and Wolf better be there too or I'll just...I'll just:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799567.gif' width='' height='300' alt='explode' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
<b>EXPLODE!</b> </blockquote><br/><br/><br/><br/>In the mean time....<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799568.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='wait' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799569.gif' width='400' alt='wa' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/486876.gif' width='400' alt='h' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799570.gif' width='400' alt='g' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799571.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='bob' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/><b>UPDATE!!!!!</b><br/>The cover for th</span>
  <span id="freeText6177467676080260181" style="display:none"><p>
  <b>
    <i>"When she was jut a child, the witch locked her away in a tower that had neither doors nor stairs."</i>
  </b>
</p><br><br><b> BEFORE READING:</b><br>Cinder?...and Rapunzel?...in a desert?...in 2014? <br>Can life get any more depressing?!?!?! It sounds so interesting but also sooooo far away! I just read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17193739.Scarlet__Lunar_Chronicles___2_" title="Scarlet (Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a> and now I have to wait a whole year!!!!<br>It's like....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399031ra/771725.gif" width="" height="" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(was that the perfect gif or what?)<br><br>Oh and Scarlet and Wolf better be there too or I'll just...I'll just:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799567.gif" width="" height="300" alt="explode" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
<b>EXPLODE!</b> </blockquote><br><br><br><br>In the mean time....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799568.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="wait" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799569.gif" width="400" alt="wa" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/486876.gif" width="400" alt="h" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799570.gif" width="400" alt="g" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408642ra/799571.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="bob" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><b>UPDATE!!!!!</b><br>The cover for these books are sooooo flippin awesome!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1375434619l/13206828.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My original reaction went something like this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/636981.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>....and then I looked at the date:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/495718.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><b>UPDATE!!!!!!<br>TEASER!!!!</b> <br><a href="http://www.marissameyer.com/book/book-three/" rel="nofollow noopener"> READ THIS! Teaser from Cress!!!</a><br><br><br><b>UPDATE!!!!!!</b><br><a href="http://www.timeanddate.com/countdown/to?iso=20140204T00&amp;p0=263&amp;msg=Cress" rel="nofollow noopener"> Let the count down begin!!!!!!!</a><br><br><br><p>P.S. Cress is sooooo gonna end up with Thorne!!!! <br><br><br><br><br><b>WHILE READING!!!!!!!! :</b><br><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392335506ra/8540568.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392313211ra/8536976.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>AFTER READING!!!!!!!!! :</b><br><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/559417.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>First WOW. How does Marissa Meyer do this? How does she create this world with all these intertwining characters and have it all fit together so beautifully? I just don’t understand!!! I could not put it down, I literally read it in like a day! I just got it yesterday!<br><br>Last night on February 12 I went to a Cress book signing in DC and actually got to meet Marissa Meyer! She is so nice and funny and just overall awesome! She always had a smile on her face and seemed so relatable. She was just great, a great person and an amazing author. <br>But ANYWAY, on to the review!<br><br>The book starts a few days after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206760.Scarlet__The_Lunar_Chronicles___2_" title="Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a> ends. The crew of the Rampion is out in space thinking of ways to stop Levana’s wedding to Prince Kai and save the Earth when they finally make contact with Luna’s greatest hacker: Cress. She has been stranded in a satellite orbiting the earth for seven years and has never since then had human – or lunar – contact other than Levana’s head thaumaturge, Sybil. So of course our heroic crew goes out to get her but things get complicated when they become separated. <br><br>Thorne is now with Cress stranded in the middle of the Sahara, Cinder is left to care for an unconscious Wolf and Scarlet has been taken away to Luna. On top of that, the wedding of the century is only days away. Though the odds are not in their favor, that has never stopped the crew before. Will they stop the wedding? Will they ever re-unite? <br><br>You’ll have to read to find out. <br>Now before I start speaking of my thoughts let me show the real story of Rapunzel (shortened version) <br><i><blockquote>Long, long ago in a house that overlooked a beautiful garden lived a childless couple. They prayed to God every day to bless them with a child. One day they found that God had answered their prayer. They were at long last going to have a baby!<br><br>Their days passed in happiness but alas! the wife fell ill. She would eat nothing and the husband was worried that she would waste away. He tried to tempt her with many good things but she refused everything. “But you must eat something, my dear,” he begged her. “There is a herb called Rapunzel in the garden next door. I will feel better if I can eat that,” she said. The husband’s heart sank when he heard her. This garden was owned by a wicked witch who would let no one enter. But he loved his wife very much and so with a pounding heart, he decided to go into the garden at a time when the witch was away. One day, finding an appropriate time he went into the garden. He had managed to pluck the herb but as he was about to leave, the wicked witch came back. “You thief! How dare you enter my garden?” she screamed. She threatened to put a curse on him. He fell at her feet and begged, “Please don’t curse me. If my wife doesn’t eat this herb, she will die. She is going to have a baby and is very ill.” The witch stopped to think awhile. “I will let you go on one condition. You will give me the baby after it’s born.” The poor man had no other way out but to agree.<br><br>He took the herb to his wife and miraculously she soon recovered and gave birth to a beautiful girl. But as per the agreement the witch came to take the baby away. She took Rapunzel—for that’s what she named her—far away and locked her in a high tower. The tower had no doors or stairs. There was only a window on top.<br><br>The only person whom Rapunzel ever saw was the wicked witch. Rapunzel grew up to become beautiful with pretty eyes, a beautiful voice, and her golden hair grew very, very long. All day long, when Rapunzel was alone, she would sing and weep.<br><br>Every day, the wicked witch came to the tower with food. She stood at the bottom of the tower and shouted. “Rapunzel! Rapunzel! Let your hair down!” Rapunzel would drop her long, braided hair through the window. The witch used the hair as a rope to climb into the tower.<br><br>One day, a handsome prince was passing by and heard her sing. He fell in love with her voice and unknown to all came to the tower every day to hear her sing. One day, the prince saw the witch climbing up the tower using Rapunzel’s hair.<br><br>The next day, the prince too called out to Rapunzel. “Let down your hair,” he said. The prince climbed to the top of the tower. After that, the prince came to meet Rapunzel every night.<br><br>Alas! the witch soon discovered the prince with Rapunzel. She pushed him from the tower onto a thorny bush, making him blind. She banished Rapunzel into the desert far away.<br><br>Many years passed. The blind prince wandered alone and finally reached the same desert. One day, he heard familiar voice singing. Following the sound he found her. They hugged each other in joy. Tears of happiness rolled down Rapuzel’s cheek. As the tears fell on the prince’s eyes, he regained his vision.<br>The prince took Rapunzel to his kingdom and they lived happily ever after.</blockquote></i><br><br><br>Now that you’ve seen that you can compare it to Cress and see how wonderfully Miss Meyer put it all together. <br><br><b>My thoughts:</b><br><br>I loved this book. I love the entire series. I admit that I had my problems with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a> but the Scarlet came and my mind was blown and just when it was getting back together Cress comes and leaves me in an even worse state than I was before and I can’t believe that I have to wait another year for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a>. I honestly don’t think I can wait that long. I just love this story and how well they intertwine and of course I love the characters. These characters have been pushed to their limits and then pushed some more. Just when you think they can’t get up they leap into the air and keep moving and I love that. These characters aren’t whinny or stupid as I’ve seen some characters be but they are strong and all just wonderful people and I love strong willed likeable characters and Miss Meyer knows how to write them so well. <br><br>I also love the characters relationships with each other. I love how they all have their matched pairs and it’s just so cute to read. Originally my favorite pairing was that between Wolf and Scarlet but I have to admit I LOVE Thorne and Cress! <br><br>In Scarlet I really began liking Thorne but here in Cress I really am starting to love him. At the signing she mentioned that Thorne is one of her favorite characters to write and it definitely shows in her writing of him. He has officially become one of my favorite characters. Part of him kind or reminds me of Puck in the IRON FEY SERIES who is one of my favorite characters EVER in that he always has that cocky smile even in the worst times and is always making jokes even in the face of death and despite that they are both really great people with hearts of gold. <br><br>Now more proof of Marissa Meyer’s awesomeness is the names!!! <br>The first is Rapunzel which is actually a type of vegetable kind of like cabbage. Now as you all know, Captain Thorne’s ship is called Rampion. In some versions of the Brothers Grimm story (see above) instead of rapunzel that the woman craves it is rampion another name for …wait for it…rapunzel!!! Then you bring in the name Cress which is *drum roll please* A VEGATABLE IN THE CABBAGE FAMILY!!!! The ship had been named Rampion way before Cress was introduced and yet it was still connected to the story! Holy God! This woman is genius!!!! It is obvious that she put in so much detail in making her story and I greatly admire that.<br><br><br>I really have nothing bad to say about this book other than:<br> I NEEDED MORE SCARLET AND WOLF! THERE WAS NO SCARLET AND WOLF!<br>There better be some Scarlet-Wolf interaction in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206900.Winter__The_Lunar_Chronicles___4_" title="Winter (The Lunar Chronicles, #4) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter</a> that is all I ask.<br><br>Oh and another thing that got to me was in the last chapters of the book. There was one line that completely blew my mind:<br><br><i> “Her warm brown skin was flawless…”</i><br><br>WARM BROWN SKIN!<br><br>Plot twist! Snow White is NOT WHITE!!!!<br>I absolutely LOVE that! I would never have thought of that. It’s just so clever and creative. I cannot wait to read from her POV. <br><br>Great book! Passed all my expecttions.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386598727ra/7399761.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>I now have a review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/523776121?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener"> Winter!</a></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="6177467676080260181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2637223958" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2637223958" />
    <a title="Meyer S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37972645-meyer-s"><img alt="Meyer S" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585401970p2/37972645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2637223958?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meyer S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meyer S" href="/user/show/37972645-meyer-s">Meyer S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2637223958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer888229536709356680"><blockquote>
  <i>"Sweet Crescent Moon, <br/>Up in the sky, <br/>You sing your song so sweetly, <br/>After sunshine passes by."</i>
</blockquote> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>Stars above,</i>
</b> this was one heck of a book<br/><br/><i>I'll be honest,</i> I can't think of a proper way to start this review other than saying that i really enjoyed this book (<i>what a surprise</i>). <br/>In fact, i enjoyed it so much that i can't find the words to describe my love for it, and for the lunar chronicles as a whole. <br/>But I think it's safe to say by now, that this is my absolute favorite series of all times. <br/><br/><b>
 </b></span>
  <span id="freeText888229536709356680" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Sweet Crescent Moon, <br />Up in the sky, <br />You sing your song so sweetly, <br />After sunshine passes by."</i>
</blockquote> <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Stars above,</i>
</b> this was one heck of a book<br /><br /><i>I'll be honest,</i> I can't think of a proper way to start this review other than saying that i really enjoyed this book (<i>what a surprise</i>). <br />In fact, i enjoyed it so much that i can't find the words to describe my love for it, and for the lunar chronicles as a whole. <br />But I think it's safe to say by now, that this is my absolute favorite series of all times. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Let's kick things off by talking about the plot, </u>
</b> <br />In this installment, We continue from where we left things off in the previous book, in adittion to the introduction of Cress and her unique story. <br />This book was action-packed and well plotted. There were always exciting events and secrets revealed, that constantly kept me on the edge of my seat, reading to find out more . <br />It was also <b>very funny</b>, And I often found myself laughing out loud at certain jokes and actions during the course of this story. <br />Overall, i would say that it was an exciting, funny and really engaging plot. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Moving on to the characters, </u>
</b> <br />In this book, we are introduced to Cress, who has been trapped in a satellite (<s>cool right?</s>) completely isolated for most of her life. <br />I really liked Cress and her quirky, awkward personality (which was really entertaining to read about in some parts). And i found her to be a great ,fun and interesting addition to the story. <br />Moreover, I noticed that there was a focus on character development in this book, which is ALWAYS a good thing. <br />We also got to know each individual character in a better - more intimate manner. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Now last but certainly not least, i would like to talk about Marissa Meyer's writing , </u>
</b> <br />I personally really like Marissa's writing style, i think it suits the story very well, <br />Her writing is not too descriptive(which i consider to be a good thing), but yet she manges to portray the world and the characters so well, making the story feel so real and alive ! <br />Now, i talked about Marissa's writing in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1132660575" rel="nofollow noopener"> Cinder </a>, <br />But i decided to talk about it again just to address the Improvement that I saw in her writing, pacing and overall story telling, which can be clearly seen in this book. <br />Also, i think it's worth mentioning that this book had ALOT of different point of views, and story settings often changed. <br />I was a bit taken off at first by the amount of POVs in this book, but as i read on, Meyer proved to be very talanted at merging all these storylines together to create a one big-EPIC overall story. <br /><br /><br /><b>Bottom line</b> is that this book was awesome ! <br />It's well written, well plotted, <br />and, well.... JUST EPIC. <br /><br />So, <br />If you're someone who is debating whether or not to continue on with this series , I would highly recommend reading this book, because things DO get crazy and exciting, <br />And i promise it's completely worth it ! <br /><br />My reviews for previous books in this series : <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1132660575" rel="nofollow noopener"> Cinder </a> <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2637223948" rel="nofollow noopener"> Scarlet </a></span>
  <a data-text-id="888229536709356680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14467746858536586177">this is the series that just keeps on giving and i couldnt be more blessed. <br/><br/>this book was a different reading experience for me than the previous two in that i knew nothing about the story of rapunzel. im familiar with cinderella and little red riding hood, so it was easy to follow along with those loose retellings, but this book felt like a completely new story to me. and it was quite refreshing not having those expectations going into this.<br/><br/>however, i was a little worried this installment would</span>
  <span id="freeText14467746858536586177" style="display:none">this is the series that just keeps on giving and i couldnt be more blessed. <br /><br />this book was a different reading experience for me than the previous two in that i knew nothing about the story of rapunzel. im familiar with cinderella and little red riding hood, so it was easy to follow along with those loose retellings, but this book felt like a completely new story to me. and it was quite refreshing not having those expectations going into this.<br /><br />however, i was a little worried this installment would be all over the place. i mean, we now have six main characters, meaning six different POVs. i was so sure this book was going to be thinly spread across everyones stories, especially since they all part ways pretty early on. but i was pleasantly surprised to find nothing was lacking. not only did i feel like each character got an equal amount of page time, but the plot was nicely developed, the pacing was on point, and it was a great set-up for the next and final book. which i am so excited for because winter sounds like a positively and delightfully insane girl!<br /><br />heres hoping my little group of cyborg, misfit, and criminal children can pull everything off! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

And who can blame her?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561778320ra/27740869.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Cinder and crew try to rescue Cress from her virtual prison, things go terribly wrong and their group is separated. <br><br>Now they must not only try to evade the Queen, but also try to reunite as the stakes are pushed even higher, with the fate of the entire Earth in their hands.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548532925ra/26974448.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the introduction of Cress as a character. Precious Kai deserves more, as does my girl, Cinder.<br><br>In short, <b>loving this series with my whole heart</b>. Incredibly happy that I finally decided to give it a shot.
